accused of having directly ordered the crackdown, an allegation she denies</p></li><li><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Hasina&#x27;s party, the Awami League, <a       <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">BBC Newsbeat has been speaking to young Bangladeshis about what the election means to them.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Sazia Mahmud, who lives in the capital Dhaka, describes the political landscape over the last year as a &quot;rollercoaster&quot;.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Since student-led protests ousted Sheikh Hasina in 2024, Nobel Peace Prize laureate Muhammad Yunus has served as the country&#x27;s interim leader.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;When the interim government started, I felt he could have done a little bit more,&quot; the 27-year-old says.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Sazia says this election&#x27;s result will be about securing a calmer political future.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;People donât want dirty politics they just want some peace,&quot; she says.</p><figure class="ssrcss-pqb4c0-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-1nsdxz9-Placeholder etlorgc0"><img alt="Young woman standing on a pedestrian bridge over a river" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/640/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/f4f1092a-4d98-4c53-a9e6-45e0c9ce59c2.jpg.webp" srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/f4f1092a-4d98-4c53-a9e6-45e0c9ce59c2.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/f4f1092a-4d98-4c53-a9e6-45e0c9ce59c2.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/480/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/f4f1092a-4d98-4c53-a9e6-45e0c9ce59c2.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/624/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/f4f1092a-4d98-4c53-a9e6-45e0c9ce59c2.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/800/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/f4f1092a-4d98-4c53-a9e6-45e0c9ce59c2.jpg.webp 800w" width="953" height="536" class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-clpeqp-StyledFigureCaption e1xtk7to0"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-15twdc6-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Sazia Mahmud</p></div></figcaption></figure>

class="ssrcss-etauer-ServerSideTime e14e9ror0"><span data-testid="timestamp" class="ssrcss-1qstrv8-Timestamp ekpio9q4"><span data-testid="accessible-timestamp" class="visually-hidden class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span></span><span><strong>Suranjana Tewari</strong><br/>Asia Business Correspondent</span></p>
      <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In its 2026 manifesto, the Bangladesh Nationalist Party (BNP) said it wants to turn Bangladesh into a $1tn economy by 2034.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The party said it will try to grow the economy through more investment and reforms. Its plans included attracting more foreign investors, supporting small and medium-sized businesses, as well as startups.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">BNP leaders have also talked about upskilling workers, selling more products abroad besides garments, and improving roads, ports and transport to make it easier to move goods.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The manifesto proposes âFarmer Cardsâ to help guarantee fair crop prices and provide subsidies, easier loans, insurance and marketing support in the agriculture sector.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">For poorer families, it proposes âFamily Cardsâ, which would give cash or basic goods to help with daily living costs.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The party also says government needs major reform, promising to fight corruption, strengthen the courts, and change how the civil service and police function.</p>

class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span></span><span><strong>Azadeh Moshiri</strong><br/>Reporting from Dhaka</span></p>
      <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Even before the polls opened yesterday, the Awami League had claimed these are not free and fair elections, and from hiding, casting doubt on its legitimacy. Now, its arch rival the BNP has been declared the winner. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The Awami League has been suspended from political activities, including contesting the elections, under an anti-terrorism law. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Would a BNP government reverse that ban? </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">When I spoke to BNP senior politician Amir Khasru Mahmud Chowdhury on the campaign trail, he said the BNP &quot;has never asked for banning any political partyâ. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">But, Khasru also questioned whether the Awami League could still be considered a political party, after its brutal crackdown on student protesters, and years of increasingly authoritarian rule. Itâs up to âthe law of the countryâ to decide whether the Awami League is guilty of terrorism, he said.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">When we spoke to one of their politicians in hiding, who asked his identity be kept anonymous for his safety, he said the allegations against them were âfalseâ and âfabricated.â </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">No matter the BNPâs decision, a major challenge for them is how to unite a country that includes Awami League supporters who feel disenfranchised and cast aside.</p>

election</span><span class="ssrcss-etauer-ServerSideTime e14e9ror0"><span data-testid="timestamp" class="ssrcss-1qstrv8-Timestamp ekpio9q4"><span data-testid="accessible-timestamp" class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">published at 07:02 GMT</span><div class="ssrcss-3zvusy-Wrapper ekpio9q3"><span aria-hidden="true" class="ssrcss-crgz56-Time       <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The Chinese embassy in Bangladesh has congratulated Dhaka on what
it described as a âsmooth and successfulâ parliamentary election and the BNP
for taking the lead.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In Facebook post on Friday, the embassy said it looks forward to working together with the new government
and âwriting new chapters of China-Bangladesh relationsâ.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Chinese state media&#x27;s coverage of the vote count has widely
cited local media projections of a BNP victory.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Beijing has been strengthening ties with Dhaka since the interim government took over in August 2024, boosting investments to bring in
$800 million. The two countries have also stepped up cooperation in the defence
and medical sectors.</p>

are splashed across the walls: a slogan that encapsulates a core issue for many young Bangladeshis casting their vote today.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Delhi&#x27;s perceived role in enabling Bangladesh&#x27;s democratic erosion has fuelled a sharp rise in anti-Indian sentiment.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;The young generation feels India has been intervening in our country for many years,&quot; Mosharraf Hossain, a 24-year-old sociology student, told the BBC.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Sheikh Hasina&#x27;s flight to India after the 2024 violence remains an especially sore point.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Delhi is broadening its outreach to the contesting political parties in Bangladesh, but observers say these efforts have done little to arrest the broader slide.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">India-Bangladesh relations, once touted as a model of neighbourhood diplomacy, are now at their lowest ebb in decades.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><a href="https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cjdjj44xxr5o" class="ssrcss-1e0jzsh-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">Read this story </a>about the rise of anti-Indian sentiments in Bangladesh.</p>

src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/128/cpsprodpb//vivo/live/images/2025/7/23/7e82925c-8434-4739-8e9c-1c7d42a02611.jpg.webp" width="64" height="64" class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span></span><span><strong>Suranjana Tewari</strong><br/>Asia Business Correspondent</span></p>
      <figure class="ssrcss-pqb4c0-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-clz1yu-Placeholder etlorgc0"><img alt="A local vegetable market in Sylhet" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/640/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/12/c8555b2e-ccca-4bb8-8db8-1e5ea0efc929.jpg.webp" srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/12/c8555b2e-ccca-4bb8-8db8-1e5ea0efc929.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/12/c8555b2e-ccca-4bb8-8db8-1e5ea0efc929.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/480/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/12/c8555b2e-ccca-4bb8-8db8-1e5ea0efc929.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/624/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/12/c8555b2e-ccca-4bb8-8db8-1e5ea0efc929.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/800/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/12/c8555b2e-ccca-4bb8-8db8-1e5ea0efc929.jpg.webp 800w" width="1024" height="681" class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span><span role="text" class="ssrcss-tzgxt7-StyledFigureCopyright e34k3c20"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image source, </span>Getty Images</span></div></figure><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The BNP will now face the task of steering economic recovery.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Before the pandemic, Bangladesh was one of the fastest growing countries in Asia, with forecasts suggesting it would overtake several larger emerging neighbours within a few years. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">But disruptions to the country&#x27;s vital export industries because of Covid-19 pulled back growth.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The political upheaval that followed the ouster of former Prime Minister Sheikh Hasina in August 2024 further dented business confidence. Instability weighed on business and slowed investment. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Bangladesh&#x27;s new leadership will take the helm at a time of stubborn inflation and a prolonged slowdown. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Inflation stands at 8.5% - the highest in South Asia - pushing up the cost of living and so prices have been a central issue for voters. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">US tariffs have also hit Bangladesh&#x27;s crucial garment industry - which accounts for roughly 80% of exports.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Trump first imposed a 37% tariff on
Bangladeshi imports last year, later easing it in stages before agreeing to a reduced 19% just this week under a new trade deal. </p>

      <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">BNP&#x27;s secretary-general Mirza Fakhrul Islam Alamgir claims his party has secured a two-third majority in the elections.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He also told reporters at a party press conference that Sheikh Hasina&#x27;s party - the now banned Awami League - is &quot;responsible for the rise of Jamaat-e-Islami&quot; in Bangladeshi politics. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">A quick recap: Jamaat-e-Islami is the largest Islamist party in Bangladesh, and the BNP&#x27;s ally-turned-rival.       <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Bangladesh&#x27;s election commission has called the election a &quot;neutral and credible&quot; one.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;I am feeling good. etlorgc0"><img alt="" loading="lazy" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/128/cpsprodpb//vivo/live/images/2022/10/6/091227a4-0944-45d9-bf02-b783371e8643.jpg.webp" width="64" height="64" class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span></span><span><strong>Soutik Biswas</strong><br/>India Correspondent</span></p>
      <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Bangladesh Jamaat-e-Islamiâs surge this election reflects a mix of structure, strategy and sentiment.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">With the Awami League barred, Jamaat was effectively the only large alternative on the ballot besides the BNP and its allies.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">For voters unwilling to back BNP, Jamaat became the default option - translating into its biggest-ever seat share. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Its previous high-water mark was 18 seats in the 1991 election with some 6% of the vote. This election represents a significant jump - 58 seats already. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The party also ran an early, savvy social media campaign, amplified by what critics call &quot;misinformation&quot;. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Religion featured prominently in its messaging. In several constituencies, rebel BNP candidates split the anti-Jamaat vote, further boosting its tally.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">As Shafqat Munir of Bangladesh Institute of Peace and Security Studies (BIPSS), a think tank, puts it: âUse of social media, use of religion and being the second largest party on the ballot are the three main reasons for the party&#x27;s surge.â</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"></p><figure class="ssrcss-pqb4c0-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-17zkhwg-Placeholder etlorgc0"><img alt="Jamaat-e-Islami party-led alliance supporters attend a rally ahead of Bangladesh&#x27;s general election in Dhaka on February 8, 2026. (Photo by Sajjad HUSSAIN / AFP via Getty Images)" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/640/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/9c95e775-d320-4070-9ea1-9a1f50fab438.jpg.webp" srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/9c95e775-d320-4070-9ea1-9a1f50fab438.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/9c95e775-d320-4070-9ea1-9a1f50fab438.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/480/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/9c95e775-d320-4070-9ea1-9a1f50fab438.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/624/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/9c95e775-d320-4070-9ea1-9a1f50fab438.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/800/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/9c95e775-d320-4070-9ea1-9a1f50fab438.jpg.webp 800w" width="1024" height="683" class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span><span role="text" class="ssrcss-tzgxt7-StyledFigureCopyright e34k3c20"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image source, </span>AFP</span></div></figure>

class="ssrcss-etauer-ServerSideTime e14e9ror0"><span data-testid="timestamp" class="ssrcss-1qstrv8-Timestamp ekpio9q4"><span data-testid="accessible-timestamp" class="visually-hidden       <figure class="ssrcss-pqb4c0-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-vu8oqf-Placeholder etlorgc0"><img alt="Tarique Rahman" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/640/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/82d108d4-8ef4-4070-9282-9e593ca12c9f.jpg.webp" srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/82d108d4-8ef4-4070-9282-9e593ca12c9f.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/82d108d4-8ef4-4070-9282-9e593ca12c9f.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/480/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/82d108d4-8ef4-4070-9282-9e593ca12c9f.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/624/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/82d108d4-8ef4-4070-9282-9e593ca12c9f.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/800/cpsprodpb/vivo/live/images/2026/2/13/82d108d4-8ef4-4070-9282-9e593ca12c9f.jpg.webp 800w" width="1024" height="576" class="ssrcss-egie1y-Image edrdn950"/></span><span role="text" class="ssrcss-tzgxt7-StyledFigureCopyright e34k3c20"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image source, </span>Getty Images</span></div></figure><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">This result is a dramatic turnaround for the BNP and its leader Tarique Rahman, who is now on track to become Bangladesh&#x27;s next prime minister.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In the previous election just two years ago, Rahman was in self-imposed exile in London, while many of the BNP members and supporters were thrown behind bars under Sheikh Hasina&#x27;s administration.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Rahman&#x27;s political career has been mired in controversy. He was arrested for corruption in 2007, and left for London the next year. He was sentenced to life while in absentia over an earlier attack on a Hasina rally, which Rahman has dismissed as politically motivated. The ousting of Hasina in 2024 saw several of his convictions and charges overturned, enabling his return to Bangladesh.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">His father Ziaur Rahman, was one of the leading figures in Bangladesh&#x27;s fight for independence. He served as the country&#x27;s president until he was assasinated in 1981. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Tarique Rahman&#x27;s mother Khaleda Zia was a three-time prime minister, although she was also arrested several times and imprisoned during Hasina&#x27;s Awami League government. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Zia had intended to contest this election but died in December, a few days after Rahman returned home from London.</p>

      <p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Pakistan&#x27;s PM Shehbaz Sharif has also congratulated Tarique Rahman on &quot;leading the BNP to a resounding victory&quot; in the elections. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;I look forward to working closely with the new Bangladesh leadership to further strengthen our historic, brotherly multifaceted bilateral relations and advance our shared goals of peace, stability, and development in South Asia and beyond,&quot; he wrote on X.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Bangladesh and Pakistan forged close ties after Sheikh Hasinaâs fall. Late last month, a commercial airliner flew from Dhaka to the Pakistani city of Karachi, the first direct flight between the two countries in 14 years.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Months earlier, Pakistan&#x27;s foreign minister visited Dhaka for the first time in 13 years. Several senior Bangladeshi and Pakistani military officials have also made bilateral visits discussing security cooperation, while trade rose by 27% in 2024-25.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It all showed the
dramatic turnaround of Dhakaâs relationship with its one-time foe Pakistan.
Relations between Dhaka and Islamabad had been frosty during Hasina&#x27;s 15-year rule.</p>
